324 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smyth


SC No. 25860


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


286 Ore. 293; 593 P.2d 1166; 1979 Ore. LEXIS 758


January 3, 1979, Argued  
May 1, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. ** No. TC 38440, CA No. 9205.


**  Appeal from Circuit Court, Lincoln County. Charles H. Foster, Judge. 34 Or App 899, 580 P2d 559 (1978).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the order of the trial court that had convicted him of unauthorized use of a vehicle in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.135 in a second trial following an initial mistrial and denied his motion to suppress witness transcripts from the first trial offered by the State under Or. Rev. Stat. § 41.900(8) based on the fact the witnesses were out of the state.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle was reported stolen in Canada. At the first trial, two Canadian witnesses testified for the State. A mistrial was declared. At the second trial, the State made no effort to produce the witnesses and offered the transcripts from the first trial. Defendant objected. The trial court admitted the transcripts and convicted defendant. Defendant appealed. The appellate court remanded on another issue. Defendant appealed. The court reversed. Section 41.900(8) was meant to apply to criminal proceedings only so far as consistent with respecting defendant's right to confrontation under Or. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. VI. The witnesses were not unavailable under Or. Rev. Stat. § 41.900(8) because the State had not made a good-faith effort to obtain the witnesses' presence at trial. While the State was not required to obtain the involuntary attendance of a witness, a good-faith effort was required. Defendant had a right not only to confront the witnesses but also to do so in the presence of a jury so that the jury was able to assess the witnesses' credibility.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court, which had affirmed defendant's conviction. The case was remanded for a new trial.

 

325 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heintz


SC No. 25913


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


286 Ore. 239; 594 P.2d 385; 1979 Ore. LEXIS 770


February 7, 1979, Argued  
May 1, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 17-023, CA No. 8026.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County, Gregory Milnes, Judge. (34 Or App 175, 578 P2d 447 (1978), modified 35 Or App 155, 580 P2d 1064 (1978).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Oregon) affirmed defendant's conviction of manslaughter in the second degree after an automobile accident in which defendant's passenger was killed. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the lower court erred in admitting blood test results because the taking of his blood without his consent, and not as an incident to his arrest, was an unreasonable search and seizure. Defendant also claimed that the results of the blood tests were inadmissible because there was no showing that the technician had a permit as required by Or. Rev. Stat. § 487.815. The court rejected these claims and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that in this situation, where defendant was hospitalized in serious condition, his consent to the blood test was irrelevant, and that the taking of the blood test did not constitute an unreasonable search and seizure. The court further held that there was probable cause based on the officers' determinations that defendant smelled and appeared as if he had consumed alcohol. In addition, the court held that the evanescent nature of the alcohol in defendant's blood provided exigent circumstances, and that there was no need to make an arrest before drawing defendant's blood. In addition, although the lab technician did not have a permit, the court held that her testimony was competent and properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of manslaughter in the second degree.

State v. Greene


SC No. 25650


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


285 Ore. 337; 591 P.2d 1362; 1979 Ore. LEXIS 909

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), which denied his motion to suppress evidence seized from a car.


OVERVIEW: A witness gave the police a description of the car and the thieves who had broken into the victim's residence and assaulted the victims. The morning after the crime, an officer went to the address listed for the owner of the car and a car fitting the description given by the neighbor, including the license number, was parked in the residential driveway. 327 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vance


SC No. 25892


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


285 Ore. 383; 591 P.2d 355; 1979 Ore. LEXIS 913


January 3, 1979, Argued  
February 27, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 077-07-09250, CA No. 9804.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. William M. Dale, Judge. 35 Or App 267, 582 P2d 66 (1978).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed his conviction for robbery in the first degree under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.415(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery in the first degree under § 164.415(1), based on an information alleging that in the course of committing theft he threatened the immediate use of physical force upon the victim of the robbery and was armed with a deadly weapon. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court determined that the trial court properly instructed the jury that if a firearm was pointed at another within firing range, the jury was permitted, but not required, to infer that the firearm was loaded. That instruction did not unconstitutionally place the burden on defendant to negate the distinguishing element of first degree robbery and to sacrifice his privilege not to testify. The burden to prove that the firearm was loaded remained upon the State, because the jury was not required to find that the firearm was loading merely because it was pointed at another within firing range. However, the State was not required to prove that fact by direct evidence that the gun was loaded, but could seek to prove that fact by indirect evidence, just as it could ordinarily prove any element of a crime by indirect evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision.

 

328 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Classen


SC No. 25703


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


285 Ore. 221; 590 P.2d 1198; 1979 Ore. LEXIS 881


June 5, 1978, Argued  
February 13, 1979 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals; * TC No. 94958, CA No. 7262.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Dale Jacobs, Judge. 31 Or App 683, 571 P2d 527 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed his conviction of a burglary and theft at a home where he allegedly had been doing yard work. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court should have suppressed the victim's identification of him at trial because the circumstances of the pretrial photographic identification were so suggestive as to destroy its reliability.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice were alleged to have solicited yard work at the victim's house and, under the premise of using the restroom, were alleged to have taken several valuables from the victim's home and fled. Seven months after the crime, the victim identified defendant from a photographic array. The court concluded that two elements of the identification process must be characterized as suggestive. One was the officer's statement to the victim that the suspect was one of the persons pictured. The second suggestive element was the fact that only one of the pictures showed a man with facial hair beyond a mustache. In her report of the incident, the victim made a particular point of one suspect's "Vandyke" beard. Only one of the photographs featured a man with such a beard. The court concluded that the evidence of the victim's identification should have been suppressed by the trial court. Because the victim did not make the photographic identification until seven months after the crime and because her identification of defendant was not, by her own admission, very positive, the court concluded that the error had been prejudicial and required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant was entitled to a new trial and reversed and remanded his conviction.

 

329 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Francis


SC No. 25618


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


284 Ore. 621; 588 P.2d 611; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1267


March 6, 1978, Argued  
December 27, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from Court of Appeals. * CA No. 7293.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Roland K. Rodman, Judge. 30 Or App 359, 567 P2d 558 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgement of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed defendant's conviction for rape in the first degree. The issue before the court was the trial court's refusal to allow defendant to submit evidence of partial responsibility and the trial court's refusal to instruct on partial responsibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sole defense was his mental state. The trial court refused to permit introduction of defendant's mental disease as to his claim of partial responsibility. The same exact evidence as to defendant's mental disease was introduced into evidence anyway as part of defendant's insanity defense pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.295(1). The trial court did not err in refusing to give a jury instruction that "tracked" Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.300. The court held that the statute was an evidence statute and did not apply to jury instructions. In addition, the instruction was in terms of defendant's "intent." This meant it was not relevant to the crime for which defendant was indicted and tried. The indictment referred to defendant's knowledge, not his intent, two distinct concepts under the state's criminal code. Thus, the proposed instruction was not appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

330 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Department of Revenue


SC No. 25576


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON, Department One


284 Ore. 409; 587 P.2d 91; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1177


September 12, 1978, Argued  
November 29, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oregon Tax Court. Carlisle B. Roberts, Judge. TC No. 1128.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought an action against defendant Oregon Department of Revenue in which the taxpayer argued that a 1973 amendment to Or. Rev. Stat. § 119.005(2) should not be applied to a 1974 gift to her son, who was 21 when he was adopted in 1972. The Oregon Tax Court ruled that the amendment did apply. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The 1973 amendment, which took effect before the gift was made, provided that if an adopted person was 21 years or older at the time of his adoption, any transfer of property to him within three years after the adoption was subject to additional or collateral gift tax. The taxpayer argued that the amendment retroactively affected the adoptee's status in relation to the taxpayer and as such was unconstitutional. The court rejected the taxpayer's argument. It stated that the amendment did not change any relationship, rights, and obligations between the taxpayer and the adoptee; rather, only the taxpayer's gift tax obligations were affected. Moreover, the court stated, because the amendment applied only to gifts made after the effective date of the amendment, the taxpayer's due process rights were not violated, as they might have been had the Department attempted to impose the collateral tax upon gifts made before the effective date. The court added that although the taxpayer argued that imposition of the collateral tax violated the Equal Protection and Privileges and Immunities Clauses, she had not cited any United States Supreme Court authority to support her argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's decree.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner sought review of a judgment by Court of Appeals (Oregon) that affirmed a trial court, which denied the landowner's request for a writ of review of a decision by respondent county to deny the landowner a permit to place a mobile home on his land, which respondent planning commission determined violated the county's conditional use ordinance, after respondent neighbors objected to the request.


OVERVIEW: The landowner claimed that the Deschutes County, Ore., Zoning Ordinance allowed for the placement of a mobile home on his land and that the county was required to issue him a permit to do so. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that affirmed the trial court's denial of the landowner's request for a writ of review of its decision to deny the landowner's request to require the county to allow him to place his mobile home on his land. The court held that the county's planning commission had the authority to establish standards by which to issue conditional use permits and that the standards created by the commission were reasonable in that they met the goals required by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 197.175, 197.250.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment the lower courts denying the landowner a writ of review of the decision of the planning commission that denied the landowner's request to require the county to allow him to place his mobile home on his land.

In re Oregon Mass Transp. Financing Authority


SC No. 25519


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


284 Ore. 241; 586 P.2d 784; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1154


April 3, 1978, Argued  
November 15, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding to determine constitutionality.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, Chairman of the Oregon Transportation Commission and two mass transit districts, brought an action against respondent Oregon Mass Transportation Authority to determine the validity of the Oregon Mass Transportation Financing Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 267.227. The Authority was unwilling to proceed with the Act's financing provisions without a determination of the Act's validity. An intervenor asserted the Act's unconstitutionality.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed the Authority's petition for the court's determination of the challenged constitutionality of the Act, brought by the Authority for a clear declaration that the Act was in compliance with the Oregon Constitution and effective as enacted. The court on appeal dismissed the Authority's petition based on its determination that, without an actual challenge calling into question some particular aspect or provision of the Act, the court was without original jurisdiction to determine questions regarding the Act's constitutionality under § 20 of the Act. The court ruled that the only disclosed controversy concerned the limits of the Authority's discretion to refuse to act, a question which involved only the Act's proper construction and not its constitutionality. The court also found that the court's decision allowing participation of an intervenor asserting that the Act was unconstitutional was in error because, in the absence of a party petition or response disclosing a controversy within the court's original jurisdiction under § 20, there was no recognized proceeding before the court in which to intervene.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the Authority's petition.

 

333 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


La Grande v. Public Employees Retirement Bd.


SC No. 25230


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


284 Ore. 173; 586 P.2d 765; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1219


July 10, 1978, Argued  
October 25, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for Rehearing Filed March 21, 1978. Former Decision Adhered to, Petition for Rehearing Allowed June 27, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC Nos. 22993, 29437, CA Nos. 5493, 6129.


*  Consolidated appeal from the Circuit Courts of Union County, W. F. Brownton, Senior Judge, and Clatsop County, Thomas E. Edison, Judge. 28 Or App 9, 558 P2d 1236 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Former decision adhered to.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent cities sought a rehearing in an action filed by petitioner public employees retirement board due to the court's order that sustained state laws that mandated certain retirement and insurance benefits for police and firefighting personnel against claims that the amendments to the Oregon Constitution were unconstitutional in that they infringed on the cities' self-government powers.


OVERVIEW: The court sustained state laws that mandated certain retirement and insurance benefits for police and firefighting personnel against claims that the laws unconstitutionally infringed on the cities' powers to self-govern. The cities filed a petition for rehearing. In adhering to its former decision and reaffirming the constitutional validity of the challenged laws, the court found that the cities' petition failed to address the validity of the retirement and insurance requirements. The court stated that it was possible for the state legislature to grant local governments certain powers to act on their own without limiting the legislatures' powers. The court reasoned that the ability of a city to legislate its own matters where a state legislature could also act was essential in order for there to be room for potential state legislation. The court interpreted the constitutional amendments as safeguarding the powers of self-government. The court also stated that the amendments did not take away the legislature's power to enact purely local laws.


OUTCOME: The court adhered to its former decision and reaffirmed the constitutionality of the challenged statutes.

State v. Warner


SC No. 25562


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


284 Ore. 147; 585 P.2d 681; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1217


January 13, 1978, Argued  
October 24, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 76-1050-C, CA No. 7784.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Samuel M. Bowe, Judge. 30 Or App 117, 566 P2d 546 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed his conviction for robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another individual were stopped by a police officer in a bar after the police officer had heard about an armed robbery in another area. The only reason defendant was stopped was because the bartender noticed a large amount of cash and because defendant kept looking at the police officer. After defendant explained why he had the money, the police officer was no longer suspicious about it. A jury had convicted defendant after the trial court denied his motion to suppress evidence seized by the police in a warrantless search of his person and automobile. The court first noted that neither the appellate court nor it was bound by the implicit conclusion of the trial court that defendant's compliance with a police officer's request for identification was voluntary. The court held that all the circumstances showed that defendant was seized because there was a temporary restraint of his liberty by the police officer, there was no valid consent to that restraint, and because it was not based upon reasonable suspicion on the part of the police officer, it was not authorized by Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.615.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for further proceedings.

Foster v. Zeiler


SC No. 25484


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


283 Ore. 255; 584 P.2d 243; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 1064


May 1, 1978, Argued and submitted at Pendleton  
September 12, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Grant County. John M. Copenhaver, Judge. No. 6869.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant justice of the peace appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Grant County (Oregon), which granted petitioner litigant's request for a writ of mandamus requiring the justice of the peace to grant a motion for change of place of trial pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 52.530(1).


OVERVIEW: The litigant's affidavit to change the place of trial pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 52.530(1) alleged that the justice was prejudiced because the attorney representing the opposing party had in the past represented the justice of the peace in matters involving the justice's court. The affidavit did not allege that it was made in good faith. The court rejected the justice's contention that the affidavit was required to allege that it was made in good faith, observing that it had never held that an allegation of good faith was constitutionally required in a motion to recuse a judge, but only that the legislature could not confer upon parties the peremptory power to recuse a judge. The court held that all the affiant was required to do was come forward with some evidence from which a reasonable person could conclude that the trial judge's impartiality was in question. The court concluded that it need not decide whether the factual allegations made by the litigant were contestable, because the justice of the peace conceded that the affidavit's allegations were true.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Academy Press, Ltd. v. Beckett


SC No. 25517


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


282 Ore. 701; 581 P.2d 496; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 961


April 3, 1978, Argued  
June 27, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Lane County (Oregon) denied a motion filed by plaintiff Illinois corporation in its mandamus proceeding to compel the trial court to quash the service made upon it under Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.035, the Oregon "long-arm statute," in an action against it filed by a resident of that county in Oregon. The Illinois corporation sought review.


OVERVIEW: An Illinois corporation sought to quash service on the following grounds: (1) The first cause of action, in contract, did not arise out of the transaction of business within Oregon pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. 14.035(1)(a); (2) The second cause of action, in tort, did not arise out of the commission of a tortious act within Oregon pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. 14.035(1)(b); and (3) The constitutional due process notions of fair play and substantial justice are violated by subjecting the Illinois corporation to the jurisdiction of Oregon. The court rejected these contentions, finding in view of the court's commitment to interpret the Oregon long-arm statute as broadly as constitutional due process will permit, and upon a consideration of this entire transaction, the Illinois corporation did engage in the transaction of business within this state for the purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.035(1)(a) and that it had sufficient "minimum contacts" so as not to offend traditional notions of fair play. The court also held that the allegations of misrepresentation as set forth in the second cause of action of the complaint of were sufficient as an allegation of a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding of the trial court in denying the motion to quash by the Illinois corporation and dismissing the alternative writ of mandamus.

Fifth Ave. Corp. v. Washington County


SC No. 25233


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


282 Ore. 591; 581 P.2d 50; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 952


June 9, 1978, Argued  
June 20, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 35-107, CA No. 5444.


* Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Glen Hieber, Judge. 28 Or App 485, 560 P2d 656 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county requested review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which held that (1) the notice of Washington County, Or., Zoning Ordinance 125 hearing was adequate; (2) a new Comprehensive Plan (1973 plan) was invalid, (3) plaintiff property owner's claims of the unconstitutional application of Ordinance 125 were meritless; and (4) the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies was inapplicable.


OVERVIEW: The property owner owned undeveloped land in an unincorporated area of the county. The county enacted Ordinance 125, which extensively revised the zoning system. The new designation of the subject property no longer allowed uses as intensive as the district shopping center the owner wished to build. The county adopted the 1973 plan which designated various parcels of the subject property "medium density residential," "neighborhood commercial," "greenway area," and "transit station." The owner was denied a building permit under Ordinance 125. On appeal of the lower court's decision finding the 1973 plan invalid, the court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 215.050 did not require the county governing body to follow strict ordinance formalities in the adoption of a comprehensive plan. The county charter then did not require that a comprehensive plan be enacted by ordinance. The court held (1) the 1973 plan was validly adopted; (2) the owner had not stated a cause of action for inverse condemnation; and (3) the owner's claim that the zoning ordinance and 1973 plan were arbitrary and capricious as applied to its property was subject to the exhaustion doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and affirmed in full that of the trial court, which found against the property owner.

Clackamas County v. Dunham


SC No. 25644


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


282 Ore. 419; 579 P.2d 223; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 913


March 6, 1978, Argued  
May 23, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. ** TC No. 91323, CA No. 6817.


**  Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Winston L. Bradshaw, Judge. 30 Or App 595, 567 P2d 605 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county petitioned for review of a decision of the court of appeals (Oregon), which reversed the trial court's decree enjoining defendant owners from using their mobile home as a residence in violation of the Clackamas County Zoning Ordinance (Ordinance), and permanently abating such use as a public nuisance.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased real property in zoning district that allowed a "single-family dwelling" as the only outright permitted use. Under the Ordinance, a "trailer house" was expressly excluded from the definition of single-family dwelling. After the owners installed a mobile home on their land, the county identified it as trailer house and filed suit to enjoin its use as a residence and to abate it as a public nuisance. The trial court granted the relief requested, but its decree was reversed by the appeals court, which held that the owners' structure was not a trailer house under the definition in the Ordinance and, thus, was an outright permitted use. Upon further review, the court held that the appeals court erred in determining that the owners' structure was not a trailer house as defined by the Ordinance because a building was a trailer house within the meaning of the Ordinance if it was designed to be manufactured in such a manner that it could be moved from one location to another, and, thus, such a structure, being expressly excluded from the definition of single-family dwelling, was not an outright use permitted in the owners' zoning district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court's decision and reinstated the trial court's decree.

Carden v. Johnson


SC No. 25326


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


282 Ore. 169; 577 P.2d 513; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 842


March 6, 1978, Argued  
April 18, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Phillip J. Roth, Judge. TC No. A 7604 04800.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtor sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed her case with prejudice in favor of defendants, a collection agency, the original creditor, a corporation, and the attorney general, in a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The debtor brought suit in circuit court for a declaratory judgment to invalidate a prior judgment against her obtained by a collection agency in small claims court. Her complaint attacked that judgment on constitutional grounds that the law did not give parties the absolute right to have counsel participate in trials of small claims. The debtor's attempted appeal from the order denying her motion for a default judgment was dismissed by the circuit court because the order was not appealable. She then obtained a judgment from the circuit court dismissing her case with prejudice and she appealed and asserted that the discretionary allowance of appearance by counsel was insufficient because an expression of the need for legal representation could, itself, require the assistance of counsel. The court found that nothing prevented a litigant from consulting counsel in advance of a hearing in small claims court and, if so advised, to submit to the small claims court a request prepared by counsel that counsel be permitted to appear. The debtor had consulted counsel but did not submit an appearance request. The court concluded that the circuit court did not err in dismissing her suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the debtor's suit.

Derenco, Inc. v. Benj. Franklin Federal Sav. & Loan Asso.


SC No. 24467


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


281 Ore. 533; 577 P.2d 477; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 795


July 8, 1977, Argued  
March 21, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Pat Dooley, Judge. No. 404-741.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borrower and defendant savings and loan (S&L) both sought interlocutory review from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which certified borrower as representative of a class of borrowers who deposited funds for payment of taxes and insurance on dwellings secured by mortgages and ordered S&L to account for earnings on those funds. S&L argued that federal law pre-empted the state law regarding use of such funds.


OVERVIEW: Borrower filed an action for an accounting of earnings on funds deposited with the S&L for payment of taxes and insurance on the dwellings secured by the mortgages. Borrower sought class action certification. S&L claimed that state common law of agency and trusts, as it affected such deposits, was pre-empted by the federal Home Owners' Loan Act of 1933, 12 U.S.C.S. §§ 1461 et seq. The trial court certified borrower as representative of a plaintiff class and ordered an accounting. On appeal, the court concluded that the type of state regulation sought to be imposed here was not preempted by any federal law or regulation until an amended regulation, 12 C.F.R. § 545.6-11(c), required payment of interest on such funds. That regulation took effect after this action was filed and was not retroactive. The court affirmed the certification of borrower as class representative and modified the order for an accounting so that it terminated when the amended federal regulation took effect. The court also held that the doctrines of laches and waiver did not bar borrowers' claims.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decree requiring defendant S&L to account for earnings on deposits for payment of taxes and insurance on dwellings secured by mortgages and, as modified, affirmed and remanded to the trial court for an accounting in conformance with this opinion. The court also affirmed certification of plaintiff borrower as representative of a plaintiff class.

Davidson v. Rogers


SC No. 25266


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


281 Ore. 219; 574 P.2d 624; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 728; 3 Media L. Rep. 2030


November 4, 1977, Argued at Eugene  
February 8, 1978

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for libel based on a magazine article, plaintiff claimant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which sustained defendant publisher's demurrer to the complaint upon the basis that the facts stated were insufficient to constitute a cause of action for general damages because it was not alleged that a retraction had been requested of the publisher and refused as required by Ore. Rev. Stat. § 30.160.


OVERVIEW: The claimant brought an action for libel based on a magazine article. The complaint pleaded only general damages. The publisher brought a demurrer to the complaint on the grounds that the claimant failed to allege that a retraction was demanded and refused as required by Ore. Rev. Stat. § 30.160. The trial court sustained the demurrer. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the legislature made available a retraction as a substitute for the remedy which the law would otherwise have provided and it did not eliminate special damages and therefore that such a limitation did not violate Ore. Const. art. I, § 10, because it did not wholly deny the injured party a remedy for the wrong suffered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the publisher in the claimant's action for libel.

 

343 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Or. Med. Ass'n v. Rawls (In re Constitutional Test of House Bill 3017)


SC No. 25377


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


281 Ore. 293; 574 P.2d 1103; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 735


November 4, 1977, Argued in Eugene  
February 8, 1978 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Statutory Proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state medical association brought an original action, naming the state insurance commissioner as respondent, seeking a declaration of the constitutionality of Oregon's new medical malpractice legislation. Both parties sought to uphold its constitutionality in the action brought pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 752.190, which was enacted as part of the legislation and gave the court jurisdiction to hear the constitutional claim.


OVERVIEW: Oregon's legislature had twice acted to solve the medical malpractice problem. Two years earlier the court had held that no justiciable controversy existed in an action brought by the association against the commissioner where both sought to uphold the statute's validity. In its second attempt, the legislature enacted § 752.190, which gave the association, the commissioner, or any interested party the right to bring an original action to determine the validity of the legislation, and a justiciable controversy would then be deemed to exist. The court had no problem with the grants of jurisdiction and standing. However, it held that a justiciable controversy could not just be deemed to exist. The court could not decide the constitutionality of the statute in the abstract against all of the possible constitutional challenges that might be made. Or. Const. art. VII (amended), § 2 required an actual case or controversy. There was no controversy here. Both parties wanted the legislation declared constitutional. The court declined to give an advisory opinion.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.

 

344 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


La Grande v. Public Employees Retirement Bd.


SC No. 25230


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


281 Ore. 137; 576 P.2d 1204; 1978 Ore. LEXIS 725


July 12, 1977, Argued  
January 31, 1978 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Allowed. Former Decision Adhered to October 25, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from the Court of Appeals. * TC Nos. 22993, 29437; CA Nos. 5943, 6129.


* Consolidated appeal from the Circuit Courts of Union County, W. F. Brownton, Senior Judge, and Clatsop County, Thomas E. Edison, Judge. 28 Or App 9, 558 P2d 1236 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public employees retirement board appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the decisions of the respective trial courts that the retirement provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 237.610-237.640 and 243.005-243.055 invaded a domain reserved to local discretion by Or. Const. art. XI, § 2. Respondent cities brought the instant actions for declaratory judgment that the provisions were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The cities, as employers of police officers and firemen, questioned the validity of the retirement provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 237.610-237.640 and 243.005-243.055, which required the cities to bring police officers and firemen within the state's public employees retirement system and which required insurance coverage for beneficiaries in case of a job-related death. The court held that the validity of a state law depended on the limitations imposed by the Or. Const. art. XI, § 2. The cities had the right to local self-government. Thus, at issue was whether the retirement provisions were addressed primarily to a concern of the state with the modes of local government or to substantive social, economic, or other regulatory objectives. The court held that the retirement provisions embodied a legislative social concern to secure the postemployment living standards of police officers, firemen, and their families. The retirement provisions did not compel local administration. The cities' employees were not beyond the reach of the state's social legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' declaratory judgment in favor of the cities, holding that the state legislature did not exceed constitutional bounds of local authority in enacting the retirement and insurance requirements.

 

345 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Oregon State Bar v. Wright


SC No. 24773


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


280 Ore. 693; 573 P.2d 283; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 772


November 3, 1977, Argued  
December 28, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing January 17, 1978 See also 280 Or 713.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Charles H. Foster, Judge. TC No. 76-1522.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant nonlawyer challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which granted plaintiff state bar's motion for summary judgment and permanently enjoined the nonlawyer from practicing law. The trial court denied the nonlawyer's motion for summary judgment, his motion challenging equity jurisdiction, and his motion for a change of judge.


OVERVIEW: The nonlawyer admitted practicing law in the past and stated that he intended to practice law in the future and to charge a fee for his services. He argued that he had the right, as a matter of free enterprise, to practice law and that the trial court exceeded its jurisdiction by enjoining the violation of a criminal statute. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, with modifications. The court held that the state restricted the practice of law and many other professions to those who were properly qualified in order to protect the public. The court found that the injunction was an appropriate remedy because it provided more adequate protection of the public interests than a criminal prosecution for each separate violation would provide. The court found that the trial court erred in holding that the nonlawyer could only appear in civil cases in justice court because Or. Rev. Stat. § 52.060, which allowed any person to act as attorney for another in a justice's court, did not distinguish between criminal and civil cases. The court also held that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 51.300, a nonlawyer could appear before a district judge who was sitting as a justice of the peace.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the decree enjoining the nonlawyer from practicing law should be amended to provide that the nonlawyer could appear as counsel in any civil or criminal case in a justice court or as counsel in a civil or criminal case in any municipal court that authorized such appearances by city charter or code. The court affirmed the decree of permanent injunction as modified.

 

346 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Multnomah County Dist. Court


SC No. 25407


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


280 Ore. 95; 570 P.2d 52; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 653


September 9, 1977, Argued  
October 12, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. * CA No. 7893.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County, Alan F. Davis, Judge. 29 Or App 917, 566 P2d 522 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was charged with the traffic infraction of first offense of driving a motor vehicle under the influence of intoxicants (DUII) under the Oregon Vehicle Code, challenged the order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed a circuit court order that held that petitioner was entitled to appointed counsel, to trial by jury, and to have the state be required prove its case beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with first offense DUII, a "traffic infraction" as distinguished from a "traffic crime" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 484.365. He requested appointed counsel, a trial by jury, and that the prosecution be required to proved its case beyond a reasonable doubt. Pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 484.390(1), 484.375(1), (2), which excluded those rights for infractions, the district denied his demands, but the circuit court reversed. The appellate court reversed again. On appeal, the court concluded that petitioner was entitled to the constitutional and statutory safeguards. The court considered the magnitude of the fine, the non-payment sanctions, the relationship of DUII to other major traffic offenses, and the retention of criminal law enforcement procedures. Although the offense was an infraction, its enforcement and punishment retained the penal characteristics of a criminal prosecution under Or. Const. art. I, § 11. The standard of proof beyond a reasonable doubt in traffic crimes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 17.250(5), 136.415, applied to criminal prosecutions of traffic offenses and was required by the Fourteenth Amendment Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which had held that petitioner had no right to appointed counsel, a trial by jury, or to have been proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of the traffic infraction of DUII. The court concluded that petitioner was entitled to the constitutional and statutory protections afforded in prosecutions of other major traffic offenses that were deemed "crimes." The case was remanded.

 

347 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stockett


SC No. 25122


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


278 Ore. 637; 565 P.2d 739; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1015


May 6, 1977, Argued  
June 21, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from Court of Appeals. * CA No. 6266.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County (No. 75-4045). William A. Beckett, Judge. 28 Or App 35, 558 P2d 1241 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed defendant's conviction for arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, described as agitated and out of control, burned down a Planned Parenthood Center after having complaining about abortions. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to give his requested instruction on diminished intent or partial responsibility under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.305. First, the court rejected the Court of Appeals' determination that the fact that the statute placed the burden of proving diminished intent on defendant did not make the statute unconstitutional. Instead, the court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.305 was unconstitutional insofar as it placed the burden of proving partial responsibility or diminished intent on defendant. However, any error in failing to give an instruction on the issue of partial responsibility was not prejudicial because the trial court instructed the jury that the state must prove beyond a reasonable doubt all the material elements of the indictment including an intent to injure the property. The only real issue in this case concerned defendant's responsibility for his actions, and it was clear that his intent was to damage the building of another by starting a fire or causing an explosion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Court of Appeals' decision and remanded with instructions to reinstate the trial court's judgment.

Oregon State Bar v. Fowler


SC No. 24646


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


278 Ore. 169; 563 P.2d 674; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 921


April 4, 1977, Argued  
May 3, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles S. Crookham, Judge. TC No. 418-805.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant real estate broker sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which enjoined the broker from selecting or preparing any documents affecting rights or interests in real property unless acting as a mere scrivener in an action filed by plaintiff Oregon State Bar.


OVERVIEW: The real estate broker prepared six documents, including four contracts of sale, a quitclaim deed, and a warranty deed to assist his client, a seller, in the conveyance of real property. The Oregon State Bar filed an action against the broker alleging a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 9.160 and seeking to enjoin his activities. The trial court granted the request for injunction and precluded the broker from, among other things, selecting documents for his clients which conveyed title to real property or which affected rights in real property, preparing such documents unless acting as a mere scrivener, and exercising any judgment in the preparation of such documents. The broker sought review. On appeal, after reviewing the testimony, the court determined that the State Bar had failed to offer sufficient evidence to show that the broker either selected the forms to be used or was responsible for the choice of any of the words used in filling out the forms, so that the broker acted other than as a mere scrivener.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the injunction against the broker and ordered the complaint dismissed.

 

349 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Kruse v. Fitzpatrick


SC No. 24601


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


278 Ore. 185; 563 P.2d 680; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1203


April 4, 1977, Argued  
May 3, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. John C. Warden, Judge. No. 35692.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pedestrian challenged an order from the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent driver in the pedestrian's negligence action on the grounds that Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.115 prohibited liability on the part of a driver for injuries to a passenger unless the accident was intentional on the part of the driver or caused by the driver's gross negligence or intoxication.


OVERVIEW: The driver parked his vehicle in the pedestrian's driveway, but left the vehicle in gear and had his foot on the brake. As the pedestrian was walking in front of the vehicle in order to enter the vehicle on the passenger side, the driver's foot slipped off the brake and onto the gas. The pedestrian was injured when she was hit by the driver's vehicle. The driver claimed that the pedestrian was a passenger and was being "transported" within the meaning of § 30.115. On appeal, the court disagreed. The court held that the pedestrian was not being "transported" within the meaning of § 30.115 because she had made no voluntary contact with the vehicle prior to the accident. The court construed § 30.115 and found that to apply § 30.115 under the circumstances by which the pedestrian was injured would have extended § 30.115 beyond the correction of evils that were the inducing reasons for its enactment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

350 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Meadowland Ranches, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


SC No. 24489


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


277 Ore. 769; 562 P.2d 183; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1197


February 8, 1977, Argued  
March 31, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. Carlisle B. Roberts, Judge. TC No. 884-964.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Department of Revenue, challenged an order of the Oregon Tax Court, which held that there was an unconstitutional discrimination in the assessment of plaintiff taxpayer's lands. The tax court ordered that the assessed value be redetermined as if the property involved was 5-3-1 "farm use" property during the years at issues.


OVERVIEW: The tax court agreed with the taxpayer that the assessment was the subject of an unconstitutional discrimination and in excess of its cash market value. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that there was no unconstitutional discrimination in the assessment of the property. The taxpayer did not prove an arbitrary and systematic discrimination or that widespread relative non-uniformity existed. The court agreed that the lands involved were unimproved sagebrush identical to some lands that were classified as 5-3-1 "farm use" property; however, that was not necessarily controlling. Rather, ORS 308.205 and ORS 308.232 required that all land be assessed at 100 percent of its true cash value. The court held that the best evidence of such value is normally the market data based upon actual sales of the same property. Finally, even if there was an unconstitutional discrimination, the tax court erred in ordering a reassessment of the taxpayer's property at any lower values.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the tax court.

352 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Dickinson v. Davis


SC No. 24722


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


277 Ore. 665; 561 P.2d 1019; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1181


January 5, 1977, Argued  
March 24, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. * CA No. 5402.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Phillip J. Roth, Judge. 26 Or App 285, 552 P2d 1333 (1976).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Public Utility Commissioner (commissioner) sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which found his order of mitigation to be unreasonable and reduced the civil penalties imposed on respondent truckers to 25 percent of the statutory penalty.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner initiated proceedings under Or. Rev. Stat. § 767.470 to impose civil penalties against the truckers for unlawful operation. The assessed maximum penalties were mitigated upon the truckers' admittance of violations. The court sought to resolve issues concerning the nature of the commissioner's discretion over civil penalties and the scope of judicial review. The court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 767.470(4) authorized the commissioner to grant mitigation on "such terms" as he considered proper, which suggested that he was granted a range of administrative discretion to identify the factors so as to lead to a rational evaluation of the facts in a specific case. The court reversed the judgment that further reduced the penalties and remanded the case because no statute authorized the appellate court to substitute its judgment on the reasonableness of the commissioner's properly articulated order. The appellate court assumed an erroneous role in making its own findings and failed to examine whether the commissioner's policies on mitigation were contingent on the facts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that further mitigated the penalties assessed by the commissioner and remanded the case.

 

353 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Wilkinson v. Carpenter


SC No. 24506


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON, Department One


277 Ore. 557; 561 P.2d 607; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1171


January 7, 1977, Argued  
March 17, 1977 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Clifford B. Olsen, Judge. No. 414-252.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditors challenged a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which set the amount of the homestead exemption claimed by respondent debtors in certain real property that was subject to execution in satisfaction of the creditors' judgment. The creditors claimed that the exemption should have been set according to the statute as it existed when the decree, not as subsequently amended.


OVERVIEW: After the creditors obtained a judgment against the debtors, an increase in the homestead exemption became effective. Thereafter, execution was levied against the debtors' realty and the debtors' filed a notice of claimed homestead exemption. The creditors filed a motion to set the amount of the homestead exemption and the trial court set the exemption at the higher amount. The court affirmed, finding that the statute provided that the debtors' homestead was exempt from sale on execution and that the exemption was not automatic and had to be affirmatively asserted before the sale or it was lost. As the exemption applied to the sale on execution, the appropriate time to measure the value of the exemption was at the time of the sale on execution. Under the terms of the statute in effect at the time of the sale, the debtors were entitled to the increased homestead exemption. The court also concluded that any indirect contractual impairment which occurred as a result of the increased homestead exemption was not unconstitutional because the increase was reasonable and any impairment was not substantial when balanced against the governmental objective being pursued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which set the amount of the debtor's homestead exemption at the amount provided in the state as of the date of sale, not at the time the creditor's obtained judgment against the debtors.

Application of Portland General Electric Co.


SC No. 24630


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


277 Ore. 447; 561 P.2d 154; 1977 Ore. LEXIS 1131; 7 ELR 20372


October 6, 1976, Argued; January 6, 1977, Reargued  
March 3, 1977 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied March 29, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Review from the Court of Appeals. * CA No. 4727.


*  Appeal from Order of the Nuclear and Thermal Energy Council of Oregon dated April 11, 1975. 25 Or App 469, 550 P2d 465 (1976).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner objector challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed an order of respondent Nuclear and Thermal Energy Council of Oregon (council) rendered under the Energy Facility Siting Act (Act), Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 469.300-469.570, 469.992, which recommended the issuance of a site certificate to respondent power company for the construction of nuclear power plants.


OVERVIEW: The objector argued that the council failed to comply with the Act, specifically Or. Rev. Stat. § 469.470 in establishing standards that the power company, as an applicant proposing to construct nuclear plants, had to meet in order to gain the council's recommendation for a site certificate. Under § 469.470, the council was required to establish standards, including standards of ability to finance, construct, and operate the facility. The court reversed the affirmance of the council's order, remanded to the council for further proceedings, and held that the council purported to adopt some standards as rule in advance of the proceeding at issue, however, those rule were phrased as demands for information that the power plant had to supply under Or. Admin. R. 345-25-001 to 345-25-049. The court further held that it was the council's responsibility to decide whether to treat all demands as needs under the Act as a matter of policy and that the council had failed to adopt such a policy. Specifically, the court held that the council had established only a minimal standard on financial ability and none on ability to construct and operate the proposed facility.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, affirming the council's order, which recommended the issuance of permits to build nuclear power plants and remanded with directions to remand to the council for additional proceedings.

Or. Med. Ass'n v. Rawls


SC Nos. 24596, 24597


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 1101; 557 P.2d 664; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 938


November 1, 1976, Argued  
December 23, 1976

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, medical association and physician, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which in a declaratory judgment action brought against defendant insurance commissioner, found Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 752 to be partially unconstitutional. Intervenors, hospitals, clinic, and citizens, cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The medical association and the physician commenced an action against the insurance commissioner seeking a decree that Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 752 was constitutional. The hospitals, the clinic, and the citizens intervened. The medical association and the physician filed motions for summary judgment. The hospitals and the clinic filed a cross-motion for summary judgment. The trial court found Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 752 to be partially unconstitutional. The medical association and the physician appealed the trial court's finding that the statutes' indemnity provisions were unconstitutional as well as its finding that a physician was not personally immune from claims for indemnity in excess of his professional liability insurance coverage. State ex rel. Huntington Rubber Mills v. Sulmonetti


SC No. 24523


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 967; 557 P.2d 641; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 719


October 6, 1976, Argued  
December 16, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Argued on plaintiff-relator's demurrer to defendant's answer to alternative writ October 6, 1976; Original proceeding in mandamus. No. A7602-02684.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ disallowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By mandamus proceeding, relator employer sought a writ commanding the trial court to vacate the order remanding a claim for workmen's compensation benefits back to the Workmen's Compensation Board. The claim had been denied by the board on the basis that it was barred by prior litigation under the doctrine of res judicata. The trial court had remanded for a determination of whether the claimant was in the course and scope of his employment.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured and filed a claim for compensation. It was denied on the basis that it had been untimely filed. This ruling was sustained on appeal. The claimant filed the identical claim a second time. The board found it barred by res judicata. The trial court remanded the action. The employer sought a writ of mandamus directed to the trial court to vacate that decision. The court disallowed the requested peremptory writ. The court found that the threshold problem was whether the retroactive provision of the amendment to Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.319 was intended to include those claims which had been previously litigated and which were held untimely filed under the law then in existence. The court found that res judicata did not preclude the second claim. The statutory language, "all claims," was broad enough to cover such claims, but did not specifically mention claims in which untimeliness had been previously adjudicated. The employer also alleged that the extension of the retroactive provision was a violation of the separation of powers. The court found that it did not have to decide the question. Workmen's compensation claims were part of an exclusively legislative plan.


OUTCOME: The court disallowed the employer's requested peremptory writ.

Eugene Sand & Gravel, Inc. v. Eugene


SC No. 24696


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 1007; 558 P.2d 338; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 936


November 1, 1976, Argued  
December 16, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 11, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from Court of Appeals. * CA No. 4879.


*  Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County, Edwin E. Allen, Judge. 26 Or App 235, 552 P2d 596 (1976).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a corporation and the American Legion, brought an action to set aside a previous decree on the ground that circumstances had changed materially since the entry of that decree. The original decree ordered the removal of a large cross from a municipal park. The trial court dismissed the complaint. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) affirmed. Plaintiffs sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that the original decree was entered after the trial court held that the city had violated the state and federal constitutions by authorizing the erection of the cross. The court further noted that the cross was never removed because the voters of the city approved a charter amendment, accepting the cross as a memorial or monument to United States war veterans. Individual defendants, who were the plaintiffs in the original action, denied the allegations of change of circumstances and alleged affirmative defenses of res judicata and collateral estoppel. The court held that res judicata and collateral estoppel were not defenses in the proceeding under Or. Rev. Stat. § 16.460(1). The court applied the test for determining whether the charter amendment was constitutional under the Establishment Clause, and determined that the charter amendment reflected a clearly secular legislative purpose, that it had a primary effect that neither advanced nor inhibited religion, and that it avoided excessive government entanglement with religion. Therefore, the court held that the charter amendment was constitutional. Accordingly, the court reversed the intermediate court's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the intermediate court's order that affirmed the dismissal of an action to set aside a previous decree that ordered the removal of a large cross from a municipal park. The court set aside the decree.

William C. Cornitius, Inc. v. Wheeler

SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 747; 556 P.2d 666; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 671

November 26, 1976

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant service station operator appealed from grant of summary judgment of the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon), after plaintiff began eviction proceedings when defendant did not renew his lease.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, service station operator, leased his station from company for almost twenty years under a series of three-year leases, which did not contain renewal provisions. Company sold its retail distribution network to plaintiff. After existing lease expired, plaintiff offered defendant a one-year renewal lease which defendant declined, believing the rental rate was unreasonably high. Plaintiff gave defendant necessary notice to vacate and commenced eviction proceedings. Trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiff. The court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that lease contained an implied term requiring lessor to offer a renewal on reasonable terms in absence of good cause for termination of the relationship. The court also held that although periodic renewals of a lease could give rise to expectations by the tenant that renewal was likely in the future, this was insufficient to create an obligation to renew.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed trial court's grant of summary judgment, finding that defendant's lease had expired and that none of defendant's affirmative defenses raised any triable issues regarding defendant's right to remain in possession after expiration of lease.

In re Rook


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

OVERVIEW: A county district attorney was accused of unethical conduct in refusing to plea bargain with 15 criminal defendants on the same basis as previously offered to another criminal defendant as long as they were represented by either of their two attorneys. The complaint of the Oregon State Bar charged that the conduct was improper and unethical in that it was prejudicial to the administration of justice, it served merely to harass or maliciously injure another, deprived the defendants their right to the assistance of counsel of their own choice, and encouraged the continuance of criminal actions or proceedings from motives of passion or interest. The court found that the district attorney's conduct fell within the plain language and intent of Or. Code Prof. Resp. DR 7-102(A)(1) and that the terms of Or. Code Prof. Resp. DR 1-102(1) and (5) were sufficiently definite for the purpose of a professional disciplinary proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the Board's recommendation for a public reprimand.

 

360 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Tupper v. Fairview Hospital & Training Center, Mental Health Div.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 657; 556 P.2d 1340; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 933


June 7, 1976, Argued  
November 18, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 11, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * 


*  Review of order of Public Employe Relations Board. 22 Or App 523, 540 P2d 401 (1975).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which upheld the action of the Public Employe Relations Board (PERB) in affirming the employee's dismissal from public employment by respondent employer.


OVERVIEW: The employer sought to terminate the employee and the PERB affirmed his dismissal. The appellate court held that the hospital's pretermination proceedings were constitutionally inadequate, but affirmed the dismissal on the basis of the PERB post-termination hearing. The appellate court also held that the employee was entitled to lost wages and benefits, but refused to grant such relief. Both parties appealed. The court reversed the appellate court and remanded the matter. The court concluded that, in addition to his full post-termination hearing, the employee: (1) should have been notified of the charges against him; (2) should have been informed of the kinds of sanctions being considered; and (3) should have been given at least an informal opportunity to refute the charges either orally or in writing before someone authorized either to make the final decision a recommendation thereon. Because none of the safeguards were provided, the procedures employed did not comply with due process and the employee's dismissal was invalid. Because his dismissal was invalid, the employee was entitled to an award of back wages and other benefits until he was properly terminated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision affirming the employee's termination and remanded the matter with directions that the appellate court order the PERB to issue an order awarding back wages and other benefits until such time as a valid termination occurred. The court directed that the lost wages benefit be offset by any other benefits received by the employee.

OVERVIEW: An accused raised the insanity defense in criminal proceedings presided over by the judge. However, the accused stated that he would not answer any questions in a psychological examination. OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion and issued the writ of mandamus.

In re Constitutionality of Chapter 280, Oregon Laws 1975


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 135; 554 P.2d 126; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 536


April 29, 1976, Argued  
September 8, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Argued on petition of Roger Martin April 29, 1976; Original proceeding to determine constitutionality.



DISPOSITION: Oregon Building Authority Act held unconstitutional, and proposed leases thereunder held invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen brought an original action to test the constitutionality of the Oregon Building Authority Act, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 276.800-276.890.


OVERVIEW: A citizen filed an original action challenging the constitutionality of the Oregon Building Authority Act (Act). The court held that the Act was unconstitutional and the leases entered into pursuant to the Act were void. The court found that: (1) the Oregon Building Authority (Authority) had no purpose other than to serve the state in a manner in which the state was prohibited from serving itself; (2) there was no independent business justification for the Authority's existence aside from its ability to borrow money; (3) the Authority's only function was to effectuate the creditor-debtor relationship which existed in fact between the bondholders and the state, the state being the sole source of funds; (4) the relationship in fact was one between the bondholders and the state; and (5) the state's role in the arrangement was retiring a debt which had been incurred on its behalf and which it had the sole responsibility to repay. The court determined that the Act violated Or. Const. art. XI, § 7, which limited the state's indebtedness to $ 50,000.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the Oregon Building Authority Act was unconstitutional, and the purported leases entered into pursuant thereto were declared invalid as violative of the Oregon Constitution.

 

363 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Olsen v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


276 Ore. 9; 554 P.2d 139; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 494


April 5, 1976, Argued  
September 3, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Edward Leavy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed the order of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which awarded judgment to defendant state, in the parent's action for a declaration that the system of Oregon public school financing was contrary to Oregon's Equal Protection Clause, Or. Const. art I, § 20, and the mandate of Or. Const. art. VIII, § 3, which provides that the legislature was to provide a "uniform and general system" of schools.


OVERVIEW: The parents' school district had less funding than other state school districts. The parents brought an action for declaration that the state method of public school financing violated the state constitution. The circuit court awarded judgment to the state. The parents appealed. The court affirmed. The court rejected the parents' assertion that education was a fundamental interest in Oregon subject to the strict scrutiny level of review because the correct analysis was under the balancing test. The court found that the poorest districts were not totally depriving children of an education and the only objective of school financing was local control of schools. Poorer districts were not without local control simply because they had less funds to control. The court found that local control was accentuated in the home rule provisions of Or. Const. art. XI, § 2 and Or. Const. art VI. The fact that other systems might provide better financing and local control was not a basis for rendering the system invalid. The court found that the uniformity clause of Or. Const. art. VIII was applied to the provision of minimum educational opportunities, which the state had met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court, which had awarded judgment to the state in the parents' constitutional challenge to the state's public school financing method.

 

364 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Multnomah County v. Mittleman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


275 Ore. 545; 552 P.2d 242; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 819


June 7, 1976, Argued  
July 15, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Court of Appeals. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Richard J. Burke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, potential tax obligors, challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed a judgment in petitioners' favor and which held that a referendum election by voters to invalidate a tax by respondent county was a nullity.


OVERVIEW: The county passed an ordinance imposing a tax on all documents transferring real property that were tendered for recording in the county's public records. That ordinance included an emergency clause. Despite that emergency clause, a referendum petition was filed and the ordinance was defeated by the voters at the next general election. The county initiated this action to collect the unpaid tax, arguing the emergency clause prevented the voters from defeating the tax. The trial court held for the potential tax obligors, but the lower appellate court reversed that decision and ordered judgment be entered for the county. The lower appellate decision essentially nullified the election defeating the county's ordinance. This appeal ensued. The court found that the county was a home rule county. The court further found that the voters of home-rule counties had a right under the Oregon Constitution to a referendum on all ordinances regulating taxation. Ore. Const. art. VI, § 10 and art. IX, § 1a applied to home rule counties as well as the state legislature. The voters were entitled to their referendum power, so the county's tax was properly defeated by the general election.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's decision and reinstated the ruling that a referendum election was proper and acted to nullify a tax that the county was attempting to impose.

 

365 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Schwenk v. Boy Scouts of America


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


275 Ore. 327; 551 P.2d 465; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 794


February 4, 1976, Argued  
June 24, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Clifford B. Olsen, Judge. Argued and submitted February 4, 1976.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother filed a complaint against respondent boy scouts in the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), to recover damages for the violation of the Public Accommodation Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.670 et seq., resulting from the boy scouts' refusal to accept her daughter's application for membership as a cub scout. The trial court granted the boy scouts' demurrer, and the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the boy scouts' refusal to accept her daughter's application for membership in the cub scouts violated the Public Accommodation Act (Act), Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.670 et seq. The boy scouts alleged that the legislative history of the Act demonstrated that its purpose was to bar discrimination in businesses which offered goods or services to the public and that the legislature did not intend to force organizations like the boy scouts to change long established membership policies. The trial court granted the boy scout's demurrer on the grounds that the mother's complaint failed to state a cause of action. The court affirmed. The term, "place or service," was ambiguous; thus, the court considered the Act's legislative history. The primary concern and purpose of the legislature in its enactment of the Act was to prohibit discrimination by business or commercial enterprises which offered goods or services to the public. The term, "place of public accommodation," was not intended by the legislature to include the boy scouts, at least to the extent of requiring it to accept applications by girls for membership.


OUTCOME: The judgment which granted a demurrer in favor of the boy scouts was affirmed.

Sadler v. Oregon State Bar


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


275 Ore. 279; 550 P.2d 1218; 1976 Ore. LEXIS 790; 83 A.L.R.3d 762


February 5, 1976, Argued  
June 17, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for Rehearing Denied July 13, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Jena V. Schlegel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sought review of an order in favor of defendant state bar from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which found that state bar records that related to communications to the state bar on the conduct of an attorney were exempt from disclosure under Or. Rev. Stat. § 192.500(2)(c). The citizen maintained the records were public records under the Inspection of Public Records Law, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 192.410-192.500.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed suit under § 192.450(2) to compel the state bar to provide the citizen with records that related to communications to the state bar about the professional conduct of an attorney on the ground that the records were public records under the Inspection of Public Records Law, §§ 192.410-192.500. The trial court made an in camera inspection of the records and concluded that the records were exempt from disclosure under § 192.450(2). On appeal, the court reversed and held that (1) communications to the state bar relating to the professional conduct of the attorney were are not exempt from disclosure because there was no evidence that the communications were submitted in confidence and it was clear that the state bar could not oblige itself in good faith not to disclose the information; and (2) the Public Records Law did not unreasonable encroach upon the judicial function of lawyer discipline and was not an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which held that the records of the state bar that related to communications to the state bar in regard to the conduct of the attorney were exempt from disclosure.
